This isn't\n736:         // *necessary* to prevent cycles, because they would eventually be sub-unified\n737:         // anyhow during generalization, but it helps with diagnostics (we can detect\n738:         // earlier that they are sub-unified).\n739:         //\n740:         // Note that we can just skip the binders here because\n741:         // type variables can't (at present, at\n742:         // least) capture any of the things bound by this binder.\n743:         //\n744:         // Note that this sub here is not just for diagnostics - it has semantic\n745:         // effects as well.\n746:         let r_a = self.shallow_resolve(predicate.skip_binder().a);\n747:         let r_b = self.shallow_resolve(predicate.skip_binder().b);\n748:         match (r_a.kind(), r_b.kind()) {\n749:             (&ty::Infer(ty::TyVar(a_vid)), &ty::Infer(ty::TyVar(b_vid))) => {\n750:                 self.sub_unify_ty_vids_raw(a_vid, b_vid);\n751:                 return Err((a_vid, b_vid));\n752:             }\n753:             _ => {}\n754:         }\n755: \n756:         self.enter_forall(predicate, |ty::SubtypePredicate { a_is_expected, a, b }| {\n757:             if a_is_expected {\n758:                 Ok(self.at(cause, param_env).sub(DefineOpaqueTypes::Yes, a, b))\n759:             } else {\n760:                 Ok(self.at(cause, param_env).sup(DefineOpaqueTypes::Yes, b, a))\n761:             }\n762:         })\n763:     }\n764: \n765:     /// Number of type variables created so far.\n766: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_infer/src/infer/mod.rs%3FL715-765"}}}

I: Interner)]\\n397: #[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\\n398: #[cfg_attr(\\n399:     feature = \\\"nightly\\\",\\n400:     derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\\n401: )]\\n402: pub struct ExistentialProjection<I: Interner> {\\n403:     pub def_id: I::DefId,\\n404:     pub args: I::GenericArgs,\\n405:     pub term: I::Term,\\n406: \\n407:     /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialProjection`\\n408:     /// without using [`ExistentialProjection::new_from_args`].\\n409:     use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\\n410: }\\n411: \\n412: impl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialProjection<I> {}\\n413: \\n414: impl<I: Interner> ExistentialProjection<I> {\\n415:     pub fn new_from_args(\\n416:         interner: I,\\n417:         def_id: I::DefId,\\n418:         args: I::GenericArgs,\\n419:         term: I::Term,\\n420:     ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\\n421:         interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(def_id, args);\\n422:         Self { def_id, args, term, use_existential_projection_new_instead: () }\\n423:     }\\n424: \\n425:     pub fn new(\\n426:         interner: I,\\n427:         def_id: I::DefId,\\n428:         args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\\n429:         term: I::Term,\\n430:     ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\\n431:         let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\\n432:         Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args, term)\\n433:     }\\n434: \\n435:     /// Extracts the underlying existential trait reference from this projection.\\n436:     /// For example, if this is a projection of `exists T. <T as Iterator>::Item == X`,\\n437:     /// then this function would return an `exists T. T: Iterator` existential trait\\n438:     /// reference.\\n439:     pub fn trait_ref(&self, interner: I) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\\n440:         let def_id = interner.parent(self.def_id);\\n441:         let args_count = interner.generics_of(def_id).count() - 1;\\n442:         let args = interner.mk_args(&self.args.as_slice()[..args_count]);\\n443:         ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args(interner, def_id.try_into().unwrap(), args)\\n444:     }\\n445: \\n446:     pub fn with_self_ty(&self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\\n447:         // otherwise the escaping regions would be captured by the binders\\n448:         debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\\n449: \\n450:         ProjectionPredicate [self_ty.into()].iter().chain(self.args.iter()),\\n455:             ),\\n456:             term: self.term,\\n457:         }\\n458:     }\\n459: \\n460:     pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, {\\n465:             def_id: projection_predicate.projection_term.def_id,\\n466:             args: interner.mk_args(&projection_predicate.projection_term.args.as_slice()[1..]),\\n467:             term: projection_predicate.term,\\n468:             use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\\n469:         }\\n470:     }\\n471: }\\n472: \\n473: impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialProjection<I>> {\\n474:     pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, ProjectionPredicate<I>> {\\n475:         self.map_bound(|p| p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\\n476:     }\\n477: \\n478:     pub fn item_def_id(&self) -> I::DefId {\\n479:         self.skip_binder().def_id\\n480:     }\\n481: }\\n482: \\n483: #[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\\n484: #[cfg_attr(feature = \\\"nightly\\\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\\n485: pub enum AliasTermKind {\\n486:     /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\\n487:     /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\\n488:     ProjectionTy,\\n489:     /// An associated type in an inherent `impl`\\n490:     InherentTy,\\n491:     /// An opaque type (usually from `impl Trait` in type aliases or function return types)\\n492:     /// Can only be normalized away in PostAnalysis mode or its defining scope.\\n493:     OpaqueTy,\\n494:     /// A free type alias that actually checks its trait bounds.\\n495:     /// Currently only used if the type alias references opaque types.\\n496:     /// Can always be normalized away.\\n497:     FreeTy,\\n498: \\n499:     /// An unevaluated anonymous constants.\\n500:     UnevaluatedConst,\\n501:     /// An unevaluated const coming from an associated const.\\n502:     ProjectionConst,\\n503:     /// A top level const item not part of a trait or impl.\\n504:     FreeConst,\\n505:     /// An associated const in an inherent `impl`\\n506:     InherentConst,\\n507: }\\n508: \\n509: impl any.\\n565:     ///\\n566:     /// For an inherent projection, they consist of the self type and the GAT parameters,\\n567:     /// if there are any.\\n568:     ///\\n569:     /// For RPIT the generic if\\n575:     /// this is an opaque.\\n576:     ///\\n577:     /// During codegen, `interner.type_of(def_id)` can be used to get the type of the\\n578:     /// underlying type if the type is an            ty::AliasTyKind::Inherent,\\n638:                 ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\\n639:             )\\n640: interner,\\n649:                 ty::AliasTyKind::Free,\\n650:                 ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\\n651:             )\\n652:       )\\n660:             .into(),\\n661:         }\\n662:     }\\n663: }\\n664: \\n665: /// The following methods work only with (trait) associated term projections.\\n666: impl<I: Interner> PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\\n484: #[cfg_attr(feature = \\\"nightly\\\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\\n485: pub enum AliasTermKind {\\n486:     /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\\n487:     /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\\n488:     ProjectionTy,\\n489:     /// An associated type in an inherent `impl`\\n490:     InherentTy,\\n491:     /// any.\\n565:     ///\\n566:     /// For an inherent projection, they consist of the self type and the GAT parameters,\\n567:     /// if there are any.\\n568:     ///\\n569:     /// For RPIT the generic pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> I::Clause {\n298:         match self.skip_binder() {\n299:             ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => self.rebind(tr).with_self_ty(cx, \n483: #[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n484: #[cfg_attr(feature = \"nightly\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\n485: pub enum AliasTermKind {\n486:     /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\n487:     /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\n488:     ProjectionTy,\n489:     /// An associated type in an inherent  AliasTermKind::FreeConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n519:             AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n520:         }\n521:     }\n522: \n523:     pub fn is_type(self)      | AliasTermKind::FreeConst => false,\n534:         }\n535:     }\n536: }\n537: \n538: impl From<ty::AliasTyKind> for AliasTermKind {\n539:     fn from(value: ty::AliasTyKind) -> Self {\n540:          ty::Inherent => AliasTermKind::InherentTy,\n545:         }\n546:     }\n547: }\n548: \n549: /// Represents the unprojected term of a projection goal.\n550: ///\n551: /// * For a projection, respectively, making the semantic relationship explicit (subtype <: supertype).\n   266→\n   267→2. **Semantic Preservation:** The renaming preserves all semantic relationships:\n   268→   - `a` (the subtype) is renamed to `sub_ty`\n   269→   - `b` (the supertype) is renamed to `super_ty`\n   270→   - The `a_is_expected` field remains unchanged as it's a metadata flag\n   271→\n   272→3. **Cross-Crate Consistency:** The same field names must be used consistently across all crates, ensuring that pattern matching and struct construction work correctly.\n   273→\n   274→4. **Print Representation:** The pretty-printer will need to access the renamed fields. The print representation remains the same (`<:`) but uses `sub_ty` and `super_ty` internally.\n   275→\n   276→5. **Type Aliases:** Type aliases in `rustc_middle` and `rust-analyzer` only rename the type reference; they don't introduce new names for fields (fields are accessible only on the struct itself).\n   277→\n   278→---\n   279→\n   280→## Verification Strategy\n   281→\n   282→After implementation, verify:\n   283→1. **Compilation:** Ensure the entire compiler builds without errors\n   284→2. **Test Suite:** Run the full test suite to verify no behavioral changes\n   285→3. **Search & Replace Verification:** Confirm no stale references to the old field names remain\n   286→4. **Pattern Matching:** Verify all pattern matches correctly destructure the renamed fields\n   287→5. **Struct Construction:** Verify all struct literals use the new field names\n   288→\n   289→### Verification Commands\n   290→```bash\n   291→# Verify no references to SubtypePredicate (should find only comments/docs)\n   292→cargo grep \"pub struct SubtypePredicate\"\n   293→\n   294→# Verify new name is present\n   295→cargo grep \"pub struct SubtypeRelation\"\n   296→\n   297→# Verify field rename - should only find new name\n   298→cargo grep \"\\.a\\>\" | grep -i subtype  # should be minimal\n   299→cargo grep \"\\.sub_ty\" | grep -i subtype  # should be many\n   300→\n   301→# Build specific crate with the changes\n   302→cargo build -p rustc_type_ir\n   303→cargo build -p rustc_middle\n   304→cargo test -p rustc_type_ir\n   305→```\n   306→\n   307→---\n   308→\n   309→## Analysis Complete\n   310→\n   311→This refactoring requires modifications to **28 files** across **9 compiler crates** and the **rust-analyzer** tool.
